          --monorail-metadata-toggled-bg: var(--monorail-metadata-closed-bg);
        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;
          z-index: 200;
        }
        .container-issue-content {
          padding: 0;
          flex-grow: 1;

        }

          box-sizing: border-box;
          width: 100%;
          max-width: 100%;
          margin: auto;
          padding: 0;
          display: flex;
          align-items: stretch;

          flex-direction: row;
          flex-wrap: no-wrap;
        }
        .container-no-issue {
          padding: 0.5em 16px;

        }
        .metadata-container {
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);

          border-right: var(--chops-normal-border);

          width: 24em;
          min-width: 256px;
          flex-grow: 0;

          box-sizing: border-box;

        }

          margin-bottom: 0.25em;
          width: 100%;

          min-width: 50%;
          max-width: 1000px;

          min-height: 100%;

          padding-right: var(--mr-issue-page-horizontal-padding);

          position: sticky;
          overflow-y: auto;
          top: var(--monorail-header-height);
          height: calc(100vh - var(--monorail-header-height));
        }

          mr-issue-details, mr-launch-overview {
            width: 100%;

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

https://clusterfuzz.com/testcase-detail/5136386931621888

<span class="line"><!---->By manual review, it is found that the window time triggered by the vulnerability is very short, so it cannot be reproduced stably.<!----></span>

#Analysis



<span class="line"><!---->#Analysis<!----></span>



<br>





1. When HistoryBackend::DatabaseErrorCallback get called,it will post a task(a) with this raw pointer without observing its lifecycle



<span class="line"><!---->1. When HistoryBackend::DatabaseErrorCallback get called,it will post a task(a) with this raw pointer without observing its lifecycle<!----></span>



<br>





2. When HistoryService::Cleanup get called, it will post a task(b) and associate the life cycle of history_backend_ to the task



<span class="line"><!---->2. When HistoryService::Cleanup get called, it will post a task(b) and associate the life cycle of history_backend_ to the task<!----></span>



<br>





3. If there are [b, a] in the task queue, the execution of b before a will cause the this(HistoryBackend) pointer in a to be released, resulting in UAF



<span class="line"><!---->3. If there are [b, a] in the task queue, the execution of b before a will cause the this(HistoryBackend) pointer in a to be released, resulting in UAF<!----></span>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>

Just to be clear:



<span class="line"><!---->Just to be clear:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





>1. When HistoryBackend::DatabaseErrorCallback get called,it will post a task(a) with this raw pointer without observing its lifecycle



<span class="line"><!---->&gt;1. When HistoryBackend::DatabaseErrorCallback get called,it will post a task(a) with this raw pointer without observing its lifecycle<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





`this` is a raw pointer, but it should *not* be bound as a raw pointer. base::BindOnce() has a feature that the receiver object of a non-static method must either be a ref-countable type (in which case refcounting is *supposed* to automatically be used), a WeakPtr, or a raw pointer explicitly annotated with base::Unretained().



<span class="line"><!---->`this` is a raw pointer, but it should *not* be bound as a raw pointer. base::BindOnce() has a feature that the receiver object of a non-static method must either be a ref-countable type (in which case refcounting is *supposed* to automatically be used), a WeakPtr, or a raw pointer explicitly annotated with base::Unretained().<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It would be interesting to inspect base::BindOnce's internal state to see what template instantiation path it's going through, but I don't know of an easy way to do that... the UaF would pretty clearly seem to indicate that logic is not working though.



<span class="line"><!---->It would be interesting to inspect base::BindOnce's internal state to see what template instantiation path it's going through, but I don't know of an easy way to do that... the UaF would pretty clearly seem to indicate that logic is not working though.<!----></span>

Agree with dcheng the post task should not be using a raw pointer, but using refcounted. HistoryBackend extends RefCountedThreadSafe too, as HistoryBackend is created on the main thread, then used on a task sequence.



<span class="line"><!---->Agree with dcheng the post task should not be using a raw pointer, but using refcounted. HistoryBackend extends RefCountedThreadSafe too, as HistoryBackend is created on the main thread, then used on a task sequence.<!----></span>

<div class="issue-diff">
        <!---->
          <strong><!---->Labels:</strong>
          
          Security_Severity-High
          
          <br>
        <!---->
        
      </div>

<br>


    


        


      


        









My current thinking is this is high severity but not critical despite being a browser process UaF, since I *think* this is a crash at profile shutdown.



<span class="line"><!---->My current thinking is this is high severity but not critical despite being a browser process UaF, since I *think* this is a crash at profile shutdown.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It would still be good to understand what's going on here though--why is this apparently refcounted object not being refcounted?



<span class="line"><!---->It would still be good to understand what's going on here though--why is this apparently refcounted object not being refcounted?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1. I looked if there were other BindOnce calls using base::Unretained() with KillHistoryDatabase(), and I couldn't find any.



<span class="line"><!---->1. I looked if there were other BindOnce calls using base::Unretained() with KillHistoryDatabase(), and I couldn't find any.<!----></span>



<br>





2. We can see that BindOnce() does appear to be capturing by scoped_refptr, at least here:



<span class="line"><!---->2. We can see that BindOnce() does appear to be capturing by scoped_refptr, at least here:<!----></span>



<br>





#1 0x560428d693d1 in base::internal::BindState<void (history::HistoryBackend::*)(), scoped_refptr<history::HistoryBackend> >::Destroy(base::internal::BindStateBase const*) base/memory/ref_counted.h:418:5



<span class="line"><!---->#1 0x560428d693d1 in base::internal::BindState&lt;void (history::HistoryBackend::*)(), scoped_refptr&lt;history::HistoryBackend&gt; &gt;::Destroy(base::internal::BindStateBase const*) base/memory/ref_counted.h:418:5<!----></span>



<br>





The BindState specialization is a HistoryBackend method pointer and a scoped_refptr for the HistoryBackend receiver itself.



<span class="line"><!---->The BindState specialization is a HistoryBackend method pointer and a scoped_refptr for the HistoryBackend receiver itself.<!----></span>



<br>





3. And I believe it's not a cross-thread race, because the free stack and the use-after-free stack are on the same sequence.



<span class="line"><!---->3. And I believe it's not a cross-thread race, because the free stack and the use-after-free stack are on the same sequence.<!----></span>

Thank you for correcting my initial analysis.



<span class="line"><!---->Thank you for correcting my initial analysis.<!----></span>



<br>





I found that there is indeed a race condition issue here causing the UAF.



<span class="line"><!---->I found that there is indeed a race condition issue here causing the UAF.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1. DatabaseErrorCallback[1,2] called by db on thread a uses base::Unretained(this) with out inc refcount



<span class="line"><!---->1. DatabaseErrorCallback[1,2] called by db on thread a uses base::Unretained(this) with out inc refcount<!----></span>



<br>





2. HistoryBackend[3] free it self on thead b



<span class="line"><!---->2. HistoryBackend[3] free it self on thead b<!----></span>



<br>





3. HistoryBackend is RefCountedThreadSafe, but it only safe for refcount it self not for this[4]



<span class="line"><!---->3. HistoryBackend is RefCountedThreadSafe, but it only safe for refcount it self not for this[4]<!----></span>



<br>





4. When the destructor is called on thread b and executed to [4], and thread a is executed to [2],



<span class="line"><!---->4. When the destructor is called on thread b and executed to [4], and thread a is executed to [2],<!----></span>



<br>





even if the reference count is incremented at [2], the object cannot be prevented from being destroyed,



<span class="line"><!---->even if the reference count is incremented at [2], the object cannot be prevented from being destroyed,<!----></span>



<br>





resulting in UAF even the free stack and the use-after-free stack are on the same sequence.



<span class="line"><!---->resulting in UAF even the free stack and the use-after-free stack are on the same sequence.<!----></span>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>

2 does increment the refcount, but you are right that 1 does not.

<br>



<br>





> 2. HistoryBackend[3] free it self on thead b



<span class="line"><!---->&gt; 2. HistoryBackend[3] free it self on thead b<!----></span>



<br>

<span class="line"><!---->&gt; 3. HistoryBackend is RefCountedThreadSafe, but it only safe for refcount it self not for this[4]<!----></span>

> 4. When the destructor is called on thread b and executed to [4], and thread a is executed to [2],

> even if the reference count is incremented at [2], the object cannot be prevented from being destroyed,



<span class="line"><!---->&gt; even if the reference count is incremented at [2], the object cannot be prevented from being destroyed,<!----></span>



<br>





> resulting in UAF even the free stack and the use-after-free stack are on the same sequence.



<span class="line"><!---->&gt; resulting in UAF even the free stack and the use-after-free stack are on the same sequence.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The sequence that leads to this is:



<span class="line"><!---->The sequence that leads to this is:<!----></span>



<br>





~HistoryBackend



<span class="line"><!---->~HistoryBackend<!----></span>



<br>





  CloseAllDatabases();



<span class="line"><!---->  CloseAllDatabases();<!----></span>



<br>





    this does a db operation that triggers an error



<span class="line"><!---->    this does a db operation that triggers an error<!----></span>



<br>





    HistoryBackend::DatabaseErrorCallback



<span class="line"><!---->    HistoryBackend::DatabaseErrorCallback<!----></span>



<br>





    post task, that increments ref count, but it doesn't matter because already in destructor



<span class="line"><!---->    post task, that increments ref count, but it doesn't matter because already in destructor<!----></span>



<br>





<post task runs>



<span class="line"><!---->&lt;post task runs&gt;<!----></span>



<br>





HistoryBackend::KillHistoryDatabase



<span class="line"><!---->HistoryBackend::KillHistoryDatabase<!----></span>



<br>





use-after-free because historybackend was deleted.



<span class="line"><!---->use-after-free because historybackend was deleted.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This could happen anytime a profile is being shutdown.



<span class="line"><!---->This could happen anytime a profile is being shutdown.<!----></span>

<br>



<br>





history: don't handle db error during destruction



<span class="line"><!---->history: don't handle db error during destruction<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Handling of db errors is delayed using a posttask. ~HistoryBackend



<span class="line"><!---->Handling of db errors is delayed using a posttask. ~HistoryBackend<!----></span>



<br>





closes all the dbs. If closing the db results in an error, then



<span class="line"><!---->closes all the dbs. If closing the db results in an error, then<!----></span>



<br>





a PostTask() is scheduled with a HistoryBackend that is part way



<span class="line"><!---->a PostTask() is scheduled with a HistoryBackend that is part way<!----></span>



<br>





through deletion. When the PostTask() runs, we get a uaf.



<span class="line"><!---->through deletion. When the PostTask() runs, we get a uaf.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This patch resets the error callback in ~HistoryBackend to ensure



<span class="line"><!---->This patch resets the error callback in ~HistoryBackend to ensure<!----></span>



<br>





this doesn't happen. This means a db error is effectively ignored



<span class="line"><!---->this doesn't happen. This means a db error is effectively ignored<!----></span>



<br>





during shutdown. Presumably if the error is fatal, it'll be handled



<span class="line"><!---->during shutdown. Presumably if the error is fatal, it'll be handled<!----></span>



<br>





when the HistoryBackend is created again.



<span class="line"><!---->when the HistoryBackend is created again.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

[M101 merge] history: don't handle db error during destruction



<span class="line"><!---->[M101 merge] history: don't handle db error during destruction<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Handling of db errors is delayed using a posttask. ~HistoryBackend



<span class="line"><!---->Handling of db errors is delayed using a posttask. ~HistoryBackend<!----></span>



<br>





closes all the dbs. If closing the db results in an error, then



<span class="line"><!---->closes all the dbs. If closing the db results in an error, then<!----></span>



<br>





a PostTask() is scheduled with a HistoryBackend that is part way



<span class="line"><!---->a PostTask() is scheduled with a HistoryBackend that is part way<!----></span>



<br>





through deletion. When the PostTask() runs, we get a uaf.



<span class="line"><!---->through deletion. When the PostTask() runs, we get a uaf.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This patch resets the error callback in ~HistoryBackend to ensure



<span class="line"><!---->This patch resets the error callback in ~HistoryBackend to ensure<!----></span>



<br>





this doesn't happen. This means a db error is effectively ignored



<span class="line"><!---->this doesn't happen. This means a db error is effectively ignored<!----></span>



<br>





during shutdown. Presumably if the error is fatal, it'll be handled



<span class="line"><!---->during shutdown. Presumably if the error is fatal, it'll be handled<!----></span>



<br>





when the HistoryBackend is created again.



<span class="line"><!---->when the HistoryBackend is created again.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1306507" title="AddressSanitizer: heap-use-after-free components/history/core/browser/history_backend.cc:2542:22 in history::HistoryBackend::KillHistoryDatabase()"><!---->BUG=1306507<!----></a>

<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.

[M100 merge] history: don't handle db error during destruction



<span class="line"><!---->[M100 merge] history: don't handle db error during destruction<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Handling of db errors is delayed using a posttask. ~HistoryBackend



<span class="line"><!---->Handling of db errors is delayed using a posttask. ~HistoryBackend<!----></span>



<br>





closes all the dbs. If closing the db results in an error, then



<span class="line"><!---->closes all the dbs. If closing the db results in an error, then<!----></span>



<br>





a PostTask() is scheduled with a HistoryBackend that is part way



<span class="line"><!---->a PostTask() is scheduled with a HistoryBackend that is part way<!----></span>



<br>





through deletion. When the PostTask() runs, we get a uaf.



<span class="line"><!---->through deletion. When the PostTask() runs, we get a uaf.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This patch resets the error callback in ~HistoryBackend to ensure



<span class="line"><!---->This patch resets the error callback in ~HistoryBackend to ensure<!----></span>



<br>





this doesn't happen. This means a db error is effectively ignored



<span class="line"><!---->this doesn't happen. This means a db error is effectively ignored<!----></span>



<br>





during shutdown. Presumably if the error is fatal, it'll be handled



<span class="line"><!---->during shutdown. Presumably if the error is fatal, it'll be handled<!----></span>



<br>





when the HistoryBackend is created again.



<span class="line"><!---->when the HistoryBackend is created again.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1306507" title="AddressSanitizer: heap-use-after-free components/history/core/browser/history_backend.cc:2542:22 in history::HistoryBackend::KillHistoryDatabase()"><!---->BUG=1306507<!----></a>

        /*
         * Really specific class names are necessary because ShadowDOM
         * is disabled for this component.
         */
        .chops-autocomplete-container {
          position: relative;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container table {
          padding: 0;
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
          color: var(--chops-link-color);
          position: absolute;
          background: var(--chops-white);
          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }

        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }
      </style>
      <div class="chops-autocomplete-container">
        <span class="screenreader-hidden" aria-live="polite">
          
        </span>
        <table hidden="">
          <tbody>
            
          </tbody>
        </table>
      </div>
    <!----></mr-autocomplete>
            </div>
          </div>
